[2:0:127,32] 4100   State Council on Developmental Disabilities - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The Council is responsible for developing and implementing a State Plan containing goals, objectives, activities, and projected  

[3:1:66,79] outcomes designed to improve and enhance the availability and quality of services and supports to individuals with  

[3:2:66,89] developmental disabilities and their families. The appointed Council members engage in policy planning to ensure system  

[3:3:66,99] coordination, barrier removal, monitoring, and evaluation.  

[3:4:66,117] 3805 - COMMUNITY PROGRAM DEVELOPMENT  

[4:0:66,137] The Council administers grants to community-based organizations that fund new and innovative community program  

[4:1:66,148] development projects to implement State Plan objectives and improve and enhance services for individuals with developmental  

[4:2:66,158] disabilities and their families.  

[4:3:66,175] 3810 - REGIONAL OFFICES AND REGIONAL ADVISORY COMMITTEES  

[4:4:66,193] Twelve Regional Offices and Regional Advisory Committees provide programmatic support to assist with advocacy, capacity  

[4:5:66,203] building, systems change, and implementation of State Plan objectives in Council Regions throughout California. These offices  

[4:6:66,214] and advisory committees provide information and data to the Council to assess regional needs and implementation of the State  

[4:7:66,224] Plan for inclusion in reports to the federal government and the Legislature. These offices also carry out direct service supports  

[4:8:66,234] for pandemic and emergency responses.  

[5:0:66,254] In addition to implementation of State Plan activities, Regional Office staff support the following activities to improve and  

[5:1:66,265] enhance the availability and quality of services for residents of state developmental centers and state-operated community  

[5:2:66,275] facilities:  

[6:0:65,292] • Advocacy services through volunteers recruited by Council staff for individuals who have no legally appointed representative  

[6:1:76,303] to assist them in making choices and decisions.  

[6:2:65,319] • Clients' rights advocacy services to ensure that laws, regulations, and policies pertaining to the rights of persons with  

[6:3:76,329] developmental disabilities are observed.  

[6:4:65,345] • Quality Assessments for individuals who receive community residential services and support.

[5:0:66,192] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,212] 3820 - EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES AUTHORITY  

[6:1:66,229] Disaster Medical Services Division  

[7:0:66,247] The Disaster Medical Services Division coordinates California's medical response to major disasters by carrying out the  

[7:1:66,257] Authority's mandate to provide medical resources to local governments in support of their disaster response efforts. The  

[7:2:66,268] Division coordinates with the Governor's Office of Emergency Services, the Office of Homeland Security, the California National  

[7:3:66,278] Guard, the California Department of Public Health, and other local, state, and federal agencies, private sector hospitals,  

[7:4:66,288] ambulance companies, and medical supply vendors, to promote and improve disaster preparedness and emergency medical  

[7:5:66,298] response in California.  

[8:0:66,316] Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division  

[9:0:66,334] The Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division is responsible for licensing and enforcement actions of all active  

[9:1:66,344] paramedics throughout the state. The Division develops and implements regulations that set training, certification and licensure  

[9:2:66,354] standards, and the scope of practice for various emergency medical services personnel. The Division also sets standards for,  

[9:3:66,364] and approves, training programs in: pediatric first aid, CPR,   preventive health practices for child day care providers, and school  

[9:4:66,374] bus drivers. It also develops standards for emergency medical dispatcher training, pre-arrival emergency care instructions, and  

[9:5:66,385] the epinephrine auto-injector training program.  

[9:6:66,402] Emergency Medical Services Systems Division  

[10:0:66,420] The Emergency Medical Services Systems Division is responsible for developing and implementing emergency medical  

[10:1:66,430] services systems throughout California, including the support of local Health Information Exchange projects that will allow the  

[10:2:66,440] state to collect more meaningful data so that emergency medical services providers can deliver better patient care. The  

[10:3:66,451] Division also oversees system development and implementation by the local Emergency Medical Services agencies, the  

[10:4:66,461] statewide trauma system, and emergency medical dispatcher and communication standards.   Additionally, it   establishes  

[10:5:66,471] regulations and guidelines for local agencies; reviews and approves local plans to ensure they meet the minimum state  

[10:6:66,481] standards; coordinates injury and illness prevention activities with the California Department of Public Health and the Office of  

[10:7:66,491] Traffic Safety; manages the state's emergency medical services data and quality improvement process; conducts Ambulance  

[10:8:66,502] Exclusive Operating Area evaluations; oversees the operation of California's Poison Control System; and manages the  

[10:9:66,512] Emergency Medical Services for Children programs.

[5:0:66,336] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,356] 3831 - HEALTH CARE QUALITY AND AFFORDABILITY  

[6:0:66,373] The   Health Care Quality and Affordability Program   provides a comprehensive understanding of health care cost trends and  

[6:1:66,384] drivers of spending and   implements strategies for controlling costs, while maintaining quality care and   promoting savings for  

[6:2:66,394] consumers. This program enforces the Hospital Fair Pricing Act and investigates patient billing complaints.  

[6:3:66,412] 3835 - HEALTH CARE WORKFORCE  

[7:0:66,432] The Health Care Workforce Program improves access to medical, mental, and dental health care providers in underserved  

[7:1:66,442] areas throughout California. The Program conducts research to identify areas of unmet need and administers grants that  

[7:2:66,452] provide financial incentives to individuals and institutions to increase the number of providers in those areas. The Program  

[7:3:66,463] promotes health care workforce diversity and cultural competency. It includes the following programs:  

[7:4:65,480] • Song-Brown Health Care Workforce Training Program  

[7:5:65,496] • Mental Health Services Act Workforce Education and Training Program  

[7:6:65,513] • Health Workforce Research Data Center  

[7:7:65,529] • Health Professions Career Opportunity Training Program  

[7:8:65,545] • Health Workforce Pilot Projects Program  

[7:9:65,561] • California's Primary Care Office, which includes:  

[7:10:74,579] ◦ Shortage Designation Program  

[7:11:74,595] ◦ State Office of Rural Health 

[7:12:74,611] ◦ J-1 Visa Waiver Program

[2:0:107,32] 4140   Department of Health Care Access and Information - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The Facilities Development Program safeguards public health, safety, and general welfare through regulation of the design and  

[3:1:66,79] construction of health care facilities, including compliance with seismic safety requirements, to ensure they are capable of  

[3:2:66,89] providing sustained services to the public.  

[3:3:66,107] 3845 - CAL-MORTGAGE LOAN INSURANCE  

[4:0:66,124] The Cal-Mortgage Program is modeled after federal home mortgage insurance programs and insures loans to public and  

[4:1:66,135] nonprofit health care facilities for construction, renovation, and expansion projects. The Program underwrites loans, monitors  

[4:2:66,145] the Cal-Mortgage insured loan portfolio, and administers the Health Facility Construction Loan Insurance Fund. By facilitating  

[4:3:66,155] access to private capital at no cost to taxpayers, the Program has improved the delivery of health care throughout California.  

[4:4:66,173] 3855 - HEALTH CARE INFORMATION AND QUALITY ANALYSIS 

[5:0:66,190] The Health Care Information Program sets standards for, collects, and maintains financial and utilization data from  

[5:1:66,201] approximately 7,000 licensed health facilities in California, as well as comprehensive demographic, diagnostic, and treatment  

[5:2:66,211] data for all patients discharged from licensed hospitals, treated in emergency departments, or having had an ambulatory  

[5:3:66,221] surgery procedure in hospital surgical clinics. This information is used by health care policymakers, health care providers,  

[5:4:66,231] health planners, public and private sector health care purchasers, researchers, consumers, and the media. To further this  

[5:5:66,241] mission, the Health Care Information Program is implementing new health care cost transparency data programs to collect and  

[5:6:66,252] analyze prescription drug cost data, hospital supplier diversity data, hospital quality and equity data, and health care payment  

[5:7:66,262] data to improve transparency, inform policy decisions, reduce disparities, and reduce health care costs. 

[5:8:66,280] 3860 - ADMINISTRATION  

[6:0:66,300] Administration provides overall management, planning, policy development, legal, legislative, information technology support  

[6:1:66,310] and administrative services to HCAI.

[0:0:66,13] 2022-23 STATE BUDGET — HHS   24   HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:184,89] 4150   Department of Managed Health Care  

[2:0:66,111] The Department of Managed Health Care protects health care consumers   and ensures a stable health care delivery system in  

[2:1:66,121] California. The Department achieves this mission by:  

[3:0:65,139] • Licensing and regulating the full scope of managed care models, including all Health Maintenance Organizations (HMO) in  

[3:1:76,149] the state, Preferred Provider Organizations (PPO), Exclusive Provider Organizations (EPO), Point-of-Service (POS) products  

[3:2:76,159] and Medi-Cal managed care plans. The Department also licenses and conducts financial reviews of Medicare Advantage  

[3:3:76,169] and Part D plans and licenses and regulates specialized health plans including chiropractic, dental, vision, psychological  

[3:4:76,180] (behavioral health) and pharmacy.  

[3:5:65,196] • Enforcing the Knox-Keene Health Care Service Plan Act of 1975, as amended.  

[3:6:65,212] • Conducting medical surveys and financial examinations to verify that health plans are complying with the law and are  

[3:7:76,222] financially stable to serve their enrollees.  

[4:0:65,238] • Operating a 24-hour-a-day Help Center to resolve health care consumer complaints and administer the Independent Medical  

[4:1:76,249] Review program.  

[5:0:65,265] • Reviewing proposed health plan rate changes for sufficient justification and reasonableness.  

[5:1:65,281] • Monitoring the financial solvency of the medical groups with whom health plans contract to provide health benefits to their  

[5:2:76,291] enrollees.  

[6:0:65,307] • Convening the Financial Solvency Standards Board, comprised of people with expertise in the medical, financial and health  

[6:1:76,318] plan industries, to advise the Director on strategies to keep the managed care industry financially stable.  

[7:0:66,348] 3-YEAR EXPENDITURES AND POSITIONS  

[8:0:338,370] Positions Expenditures

[6:0:66,430] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,449] 3870 - HEALTH PLAN PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,470] The Health Plan Program's primary objective is to regulate managed health care plans and assist consumers to resolve  

[7:1:66,480] disputes with health plans. The program's key functions to achieve this objective are to: license managed health care plans,  

[7:2:66,490] conduct routine and non-routine financial exams and medical surveys, review proposed premium rate increases, assist  

[7:3:66,500] consumers with health care issues and enable managed health care patients to receive the medical care and services to which  

[7:4:66,510] they are entitled, and operate a consumer services toll-free complaint line (1-888-466-2219).

[7:0:198,365] 4170   California Department of Aging  

[8:0:66,386] The Department of Aging's mission is to transform aging for individuals, families, and communities by leading innovative  

[8:1:66,397] programs, planning, policies, and partnerships that increase choices, equity, and well-being for all Californians as we age.  

[8:2:66,414] As the federally designated State Unit on Aging, the Department administers federal Older Americans Act programs that  

[9:0:66,424] provide a wide variety of community-based supportive services, administers the Health Insurance Counseling and Advocacy  

[10:0:66,435] Program that provides individualized counseling to Medicare beneficiaries, and administers and oversees the development and  

[10:1:66,445] expansion of the Aging and Disability Resource Connection program to provide person centered care to older adults and adults  

[10:2:66,455] living with disabilities. The Department also administers two Medi-Cal programs; it contracts directly with agencies that operate  

[10:3:66,465] the Multipurpose Senior Services Program (MSSP) and provides oversight for the MSSP waiver and certifies Community-

[10:4:66,475] Based Adult Services centers for participation in Medi-Cal. The Department administers most of these programs through  

[10:5:66,486] contracts with the State's 33 local Area Agencies on Aging. At the local level, Area Agencies on Aging contract for and  

[11:0:66,496] coordinate this array of community-based services to older adults, adults with disabilities, family caregivers, and residents of  

[11:1:66,506] long-term care facilities.

[5:0:66,467] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,487] 3890 - NUTRITION  

[6:0:66,504] The Nutrition Program provides nutritionally balanced meals, nutrition education, and nutrition counseling to individuals 60  

[6:1:66,515] years of age or older. In addition to promoting better health through improved nutrition, the program focuses on reducing the  

[6:2:66,525] isolation of the elderly and providing a link to other social and supportive services such as transportation, information and  

[6:3:66,535] assistance, employment, and education.  

[6:4:66,553] 3895 - SENIOR COMMUNITY EMPLOYMENT SERVICE  

[7:0:66,573] The federal Senior Community Service Employment Program, Title V of the Older Americans Act, provides part-time subsidized  

[7:1:66,583] training and employment in community service agencies for low-income persons 55 years of age and older. The program also  

[7:2:66,593] promotes transition to unsubsidized employment.  

[7:3:66,611] 3900 - SUPPORTIVE SERVICES  

[8:0:66,629] This program provides supportive services in the community to adults 60 years of age or older, their family caregivers,  

[8:1:66,639] grandparents caring for grandchildren, and residents of long-term care facilities. Services include information and assistance,  

[8:2:66,649] legal assistance, transportation, respite in-home support, senior center activities, elder abuse prevention, and the Long-Term  

[8:3:66,659] Care Ombudsman. Older Americans Act Titles III and VII fund these services to enable individuals to access the support  

[8:4:66,670] necessary for them to remain independent in their communities, continue in their caregiving role, and/or receive long-term care  

[8:5:66,680] services appropriate to their needs.  

[8:6:66,698] 3905 - COMMUNITY-BASED PROGRAMS AND PROJECTS  

[9:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:163,32] 4170   California Department of Aging - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] This program includes the community-based Health Insurance Counseling and Advocacy Program (HICAP). HICAP provides  

[3:1:66,79] personalized counseling, community education, and outreach events for Medicare beneficiaries. HICAP is the primary local  

[3:2:66,89] source for accurate and objective information and assistance with Medicare benefits, prescription drug plans, and health plans.  

[3:3:66,107] 3910 - MEDI-CAL PROGRAMS  

[4:0:66,124] This program includes oversight of the Multipurpose Senior Services Program (MSSP) and Community-Based Adult Services  

[4:1:66,135] (CBAS) program. Under a 1915(c) Medicaid home and community-based services waiver, MSSP provides health and social  

[4:2:66,145] care management to prevent premature and unnecessary long-term care institutionalization of frail adults aged 65 or older who  

[4:3:66,155] otherwise would be placed in a nursing facility. CBAS is a community-based day health program that provides services to  

[4:4:66,165] adults 18 years of age or over who are at risk of needing institutional care due to chronic medical, cognitive, or mental health  

[4:5:66,175] conditions and/or disabilities. The Department certifies CBAS centers for participation in the Medi-Cal Program.  

[4:6:66,193] 3915 - POLICY AND PLANNING  

[5:0:66,211] This program is responsible for Aging policy research, analysis, and development for the State’s Aging programs. The program  

[5:1:66,221] specifically addresses policy and planning related to inclusion and isolation prevention, equity-in-aging, housing and livable  

[5:2:66,231] communities, and health in the home and community.

[3:0:66,69] on the development of the State Plan on Aging and monitors Plan implementation. As part of its information-gathering

[3:3:66,99] Justice Coordinating Council, Disability and Aging Community Living Advisory Committee, Equity in Aging Advisory Committee,  

[3:4:66,109] Data Exchange Framework Stakeholder Advisory Committee and Aging and Disability Resource Connection Advisory  

[3:5:66,120] Committee. The Commission also provides administrative support for the Area Agency on Aging Advisory Councils of  

[3:6:66,130] California, which is supported solely by voluntary contributions made through a check-off box included on the State income tax  

[3:7:66,140] form.

[4:0:169,122] 4260   State Department of Health Care Services  

[5:0:66,144] The mission of the State Department of Health Care Services (DHCS) is to provide Californians with access to affordable,  

[6:0:66,154] integrated, high-quality health care, including medical, dental, mental health, substance use treatment services, and long-term  

[6:1:66,164] care. To fulfill its mission, DHCS finances and administers a number of individual health care service delivery programs,  

[7:0:66,174] including the state's Medicaid Program (Medi-Cal), which provides health care services to low-income persons and families  

[7:1:66,185] who meet defined eligibility requirements.

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:412,13] 2022-23 STATE BUDGET — HHS   59 

[2:0:134,32] 4260   State Department of Health Care Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] Medi-Cal is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income Californians. Medi-Cal  

[3:1:66,79] provides access to high-quality health care services in a fiscally prudent manner through both fee-for-service and managed  

[3:2:66,89] care delivery systems. Medi-Cal activities are carried out through the following functional groups: Health Care Benefits and  

[3:3:66,99] Eligibility; Health Care Delivery Systems; Health Care Financing; Behavioral Health; Audits and Investigations; Enterprise Data  

[3:4:66,109] and Information Management; and Program Operations.  

[3:5:66,127] 3960023 - CHILDREN'S MEDICAL SERVICES  

[4:0:66,145] Children's Medical Services is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income and  

[4:1:66,155] seriously ill children, including the Child Health and Disability Prevention Program, the Genetically Handicapped Persons  

[4:2:66,165] Program, and the California Children's Services Program. These services are provided through Health Care Delivery Systems’  

[4:3:66,175] Integrated Systems of Care Division.  

[5:0:66,193] 3960032 - PRIMARY, RURAL, AND INDIAN HEALTH  

[6:0:66,211] Primary, Rural, and Indian Health is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care to Californians in rural  

[6:1:66,221] areas and to underserved populations through the following programs: Indian Health Program, American Indian Maternal  

[6:2:66,231] Support Services, and Tribal Emergency Preparedness Program.  

[6:3:66,249] 3960050 - OTHER CARE SERVICES  

[7:0:66,267] The Department is also responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of non-Medi-Cal community health services;  

[7:1:66,277] mental health and substance use disorder services; cancer screening services to low-income, under-insured, or uninsured  

[7:2:66,287] individuals; and prostate cancer treatment services to low-income, under-insured, or uninsured men. These services are  

[7:3:66,297] provided through the   Behavioral Health Community   Services Division, Behavioral Health Licensing and Certification Division,  

[7:4:66,307] the Every Woman Counts Program, and the Prostate Cancer Treatment Program.

[6:0:207,263] 4265   Department of Public Health  

[7:0:66,284] The California Department of Public Health (DPH) is dedicated to optimizing the health and well-being of all Californians  

[7:1:66,294] through the following core activities:  

[7:2:65,312] • Protecting the public from communicable diseases.  

[8:0:65,328] • Protecting the public from unhealthy and unsafe environments, and improving social determinants of health and healthy  

[8:1:76,338] communities.  

[9:0:65,355] • Preventing disease, injury, disability, and premature death; and reducing or eliminating health disparities by embedding  

[9:1:76,365] health and mental health equity language, tools, and approaches into all public health and partner agency policies, practices,  

[9:2:76,375] programs, systems, and resource allocation.  

[9:3:65,391] • Preparing for and responding to public health emergencies.  

[10:0:65,407] • Producing and disseminating data to evaluate population health status; inform people, institutions and communities; and to  

[10:1:76,418] guide public health strategies, programs, and actions.  

[11:0:65,434] • Promoting healthy lifestyles for individuals and families in their communities and workplaces.  

[11:1:65,450] • Providing access to quality, population-based health services.  

[12:0:66,468] Because DPH's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to support  

[12:1:66,478] this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[5:0:66,223] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,242] 4040010 - Emergency Preparedness  

[7:0:66,260] The Emergency Preparedness program provides expertise, leadership, and dedicated support for the coordination of  

[7:1:66,270] emergency planning, preparedness, response, and recovery efforts for all public health emergencies and disasters, including  

[7:2:66,280] natural disasters, acts of terrorism, and infectious diseases. The program plans and supports medical care and public health  

[7:3:66,290] systems to plan for and respond to medical surge; coordinates and facilitates efforts between federal, state, and local entities;  

[7:4:66,300] and other needs during emergencies and disasters. The program also administers federal and state funds to support public  

[7:5:66,311] health emergency preparedness and response activities at the local level.  

[8:0:66,328] 4045 - PUBLIC AND ENVIRONMENTAL HEALTH  

[9:0:66,346] The Public and Environmental Health programs provide public health services of: communicable disease control; chronic  

[9:1:66,356] disease and injury prevention; environmental public health; maternal, child, and family health; and vital records. These  

[9:2:66,366] programs function as part of the greater public health system throughout California.  

[10:0:66,384] 4045010 - Healthy Communities  

[11:0:66,402] The Healthy Communities program works to prevent and control chronic diseases such as cancer, cardiovascular diseases,  

[11:1:66,412] asthma, Alzheimer's, and diabetes; to reduce the prevalence of obesity; to reduce tobacco use; to improve oral health through  

[11:2:66,422] prevention, education, and community efforts; to provide training programs for the public health workforce; to prevent and  

[11:3:66,432] control injuries, violence, deaths, and diseases related to behavioral, environmental, and occupational factors; to promote and  

[11:4:66,443] support safe, equitable, and healthy environments in communities and workplaces; and to prevent substance and gambling  

[11:5:66,453] addiction and treat gambling disorder. This program includes the California Tobacco Control Branch, Childhood Lead Poisoning  

[11:6:66,463] Prevention Branch, Chronic Disease Control Branch, Chronic Disease Surveillance and Research Branch, Environmental  

[11:7:66,473] Health Laboratory Branch, Environmental Health Investigations Branch, Nutrition Education and Obesity Prevention Branch,  

[11:8:66,483] Occupational Health Branch, Injury and Violence Prevention Branch, Substance and Addiction Prevention Branch, and the  

[11:9:66,494] Office of Oral Health.  

[12:0:66,511] 4045023 - Infectious Diseases  

[13:0:66,529] The Infectious Diseases program works to prevent and control infectious diseases such as: HIV/AIDS, viral hepatitis, influenza  

[13:1:66,539] and other vaccine-preventable illnesses, sexually transmitted diseases, tuberculosis, emerging infections, and foodborne  

[13:2:66,549] illnesses. This program includes the Division of Communicable Disease Control, the Office of AIDS, the Office of Binational  

[13:3:66,560] Border Health, and the Office of Refugee Health.  

[14:0:66,577] 4045032 - Family Health  

[15:0:66,595] The Family Health program works to improve the health and well-being of pregnant people, children and youth as well as  

[15:1:66,605] reduce disparities in perinatal health outcomes. This program includes the Genetic Disease Screening Program (GDSP);  

[15:2:66,615] Maternal, Child, and Adolescent Health (MCAH); and the Special Supplemental Nutrition Program for Women, Infants, and  

[15:3:66,626] Children (WIC).  

[16:0:66,643] 4045041 - Health Statistics and Informatics  

[17:0:66,661] The Health Statistics and Informatics program works to improve the public’s health by managing information systems and  

[17:1:66,671] facilitating the collection, validation, analysis, and dissemination of health statistics and demographic information on the  

[17:2:66,681] California population. This program includes Vital Records and Public Health Informatics.  

[18:0:66,699] 4045050 - County Health Services  

[19:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,69] The County Health Services program supports county-based public health information and services, including the Medical  

[3:1:66,79] Marijuana Identification Card Program.  

[3:2:66,97] 4045059 - Environmental Health  

[4:0:66,114] The Environmental Health program works to protect and improve the health of all California residents by utilizing inspection,  

[4:1:66,124] laboratory, technical assistance, regulatory, investigation, and/or emergency response activities to improve the safety of foods,  

[4:2:66,135] industrial hemp products, drugs, and medical devices; conduct underage tobacco enforcement; oversee the use of radiation  

[4:3:66,145] and radioactive materials; regulate medical waste; and conduct other environmental management programs. The program  

[4:4:66,155] includes the Division of Food and Drug Safety and the Division of Radiation Safety and Environmental Management.  

[4:5:66,173] 4050 - LICENSING AND CERTIFICATION  

[4:6:66,190] 4050010 - Health Facilities  

[5:0:66,208] The Health Facilities program regulates the quality of care in over 12,000 public and private health facilities, clinics, and  

[5:1:66,218] agencies throughout the state; licenses nursing home administrators; certifies nurse assistants, home health aides, and  

[5:2:66,229] hemodialysis technicians; and oversees the prevention, surveillance and reporting of healthcare-associated infections in  

[5:3:66,239] California's health facilities.  

[5:4:66,256] 4050019 - Laboratory Field Services  

[6:0:66,274] The Laboratory Field Services   program regulates California clinical and public health laboratory, blood bank, biologics, and  

[6:1:66,284] tissue bank quality standards through licensure and oversight of approximately 22,000 clinical laboratories, public health  

[6:2:66,295] laboratories, blood banks, biologics facilities, and tissue banks operating in California; and approximately 60,000 California  

[6:3:66,305] laboratory personnel in more than 30 different categories of laboratory personnel including phlebotomists, cytotechnologists,  

[6:4:66,315] medical laboratory technicians, clinical laboratory scientists, and public health microbiologists.  

[6:5:66,333] 9900 - DEPARTMENTAL ADMINISTRATION  

[7:0:66,350] This program provides overall management, planning, policy development, and administrative support services for all DPH  

[7:1:66,361] programs. This program is carried out by the Director's Office, the Office of Health Equity, the Office of Compliance, the Office  

[7:2:66,371] of Policy and Planning, the Strategic Development & External Relations Fusion Center, the Office of Communications, the  

[7:3:66,381] Office of Professional Development and Engagement, the Office of Legal Services, Legislative and Governmental Affairs, the  

[7:4:66,391] Information Technology Services Division, the Human Resources Division, and the Administration Division.

[10:0:66,596] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[11:0:66,615] The Department of Public Health operates a single laboratory facility in Richmond, California. The laboratory provides  

[11:1:66,625] analytical, diagnostic, developmental, evaluative, epidemiological, reference, quality control, educational, training, and  

[12:0:66,636] consultative laboratory services related to the protection and promotion of public health. The Richmond campus consists of  

[12:1:66,646] 697,000 gross square feet of laboratory, office, and support facilities on 29 acres.

[9:0:176,361] 4300   Department of Developmental Services  

[10:0:66,382] The Department of Developmental Services is responsible under the Lanterman Developmental Disabilities Services Act for  

[10:1:66,393] overseeing the coordination and delivery of services and supports that persons with developmental disabilities need to lead  

[10:2:66,403] more independent and productive lives and to make choices and decisions about their lives. The Department sets broad policy  

[10:3:66,413] and provides leadership for developmental services statewide; establishes priorities and standards within which the  

[10:4:66,423] developmental services program operates; monitors, reviews, and evaluates service delivery; and helps to remediate problems  

[10:5:66,433] that arise. Services are delivered through a statewide network of 21 private, nonprofit, locally based community agencies  

[10:6:66,444] known as regional centers as well as through state-operated facilities. The Department, through contracts with the 21 regional  

[10:7:66,454] centers, oversees through audits and other review the coordination of services to persons with developmental disabilities;  

[10:8:66,464] provides that such services are planned, provided, and meet the needs and choices of these individuals at each stage of their  

[10:9:66,474] lives; and, to the extent possible, accomplishes these goals in the individual's home community.  

[11:0:66,492] Because the Department of Developmental Services' programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has  

[11:1:66,502] a capital outlay program to support this need. For specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure  

[11:2:66,512] Overview."

[7:0:66,413] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[8:0:66,432] 4140 - COMMUNITY SERVICES PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,452] Through the network of regional centers, the Department contracts with regional centers to support the development and  

[9:1:66,463] maintenance of services for eligible persons with developmental disabilities who reside in the community. The regional centers  

[9:2:66,473] directly provide or coordinate the following services and supports: (1) information and referral, (2) assessment and diagnosis,  

[9:3:66,483] (3) counseling, (4) lifelong individualized planning and service coordination, (5) purchase of necessary services included in the  

[9:4:66,493] individual program plan, (6) assistance in finding and using community and other resources, (7) advocacy for the protection of  

[9:5:66,503] legal, civil, and service rights, (8) early intervention services for infants and their families, (9) family support, (10) planning,  

[9:6:66,514] placement, and monitoring for 24-hour out-of-home care, (11) training and educational opportunities for individuals and families,  

[9:7:66,524] (12) community education about developmental disabilities, and (13) habilitation services.  

[10:0:66,542] 4145 - STATE-OPERATED RESIDENTIAL AND COMMUNITY FACILITIES PROGRAM  

[11:0:66,559] The Department currently operates two residential facilities: Fairview Developmental Center (Orange County) and Porterville  

[11:1:66,569] Developmental Center (Tulare County). Secure treatment services are provided at the Porterville Developmental Center  

[11:2:66,580] for   individuals who have been found incompetent to stand trial due to their developmental disability or are dangerous to  

[11:3:66,590] themselves or others and civilly committed to the facility by court order. The Department is projected to operate seven  

[11:4:66,600] Stabilization, Training, Assistance, and Reintegration (STAR) residences in Northern, Central, and Southern California   to  

[11:5:66,610] provide acute crisis services in the community. The Department also leases one small community facility for persons who  

[11:6:66,620] require specialized behavioral interventions: Canyon Springs, a 63-bed facility in Cathedral City (Riverside County).  

[12:0:66,638] All   residential facilities are licensed as General Acute Care Hospitals with distinct parts for skilled nursing care and intermediate  

[12:1:66,648] care. Canyon Springs operates as an intermediate care facility and STAR residences operate as community crisis homes.  

[12:2:66,659] Services at all facilities involve the provision of active treatment through residential and day programs on a 24-hour basis,  

[12:3:66,669] including appropriate medical and dental care, health maintenance activities, and assistance with activities of daily living,  

[12:4:66,679] training, education, and employment.  

[13:0:66,697] Individuals served in the STAR crisis   residences are committed by a court order to the Department for suitable treatment and  

[13:1:66,707] habilitation services during a crisis and are provided services and supports necessary to prepare them for return to their  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,69] residential home or to transition to a new living option. The primary objective of this program   is to provide a safety net of  

[3:1:66,79] services that include providing care, treatment, crisis services, and habilitation services to residents based upon assessed  

[3:2:66,89] need and as outlined in each person's Individual Program Plan. These services are offered in the most efficient, effective, and  

[3:3:66,99] least restrictive manner to all individuals referred by the regional centers and/or the judicial system and are designed to teach  

[3:4:66,109] individuals the skills for increased independence, provide for preservation or improvement of health and welfare, and enhance  

[3:5:66,120] personal competence in all areas of daily living.  

[3:6:66,137] 4149 - PROGRAM ADMINISTRATION  

[4:0:66,158] The objective of this program is to: (1) provide overall management, planning and policy development, legal, legislative, audit,  

[4:1:66,168] and administrative services; (2) manage revenue and reimbursement collections from federal and state programs, insurance  

[4:2:66,178] companies, and private payers for the cost of services; (3) monitor regional center operations for compliance with statute,  

[4:3:66,188] regulations, and their contract with the Department; (4) provide central administrative and clinical management services to  

[4:4:66,199] the   state-operated residential and community   facilities to oversee the quality of services provided, compliance with state  

[4:5:66,209] licensing and federal certification requirements, protection of consumers and staff, and maintenance of facility structures and  

[4:6:66,219] grounds; and (5) oversee areas that include the development of policies and procedures for developmental center operations,  

[4:7:66,229] law enforcement and protective services, facility population management, program and fiscal oversight, and facility planning  

[4:8:66,239] and support.

[7:0:66,436] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[7:1:66,455] The Department of Developmental Services is responsible for the operation and maintenance of facilities under its control,  

[7:2:66,465] including two state-owned and operated 24-hour care facilities and related buildings, grounds, and infrastructure. The facilities  

[7:3:66,475] are Fairview Developmental Center in Orange County and Porterville Developmental Center in Tulare County.  

[7:4:66,493] The developmental centers are comprised of approximately 2.3 million gross square feet in 319 buildings on 784 acres. As of  

[7:5:66,503] February 2020, the Fairview Developmental Center and the Porterville General Treatment Area transitioned all former residents  

[7:6:66,514] to community living. The Department will continue to maintain the Fairview property in warm shutdown mode until disposition of  

[7:7:66,524] the property. The Department is projected to operate seven Stabilization, Training, Assistance, and Reintegration (STAR)  

[7:8:66,534] residences that provide acute crisis services in the community. Additionally, the Department is responsible for the maintenance  

[7:9:66,544] of interior finishes and equipment at Canyon Springs, a 57,000-square-foot leased facility in Riverside County. These facilities  

[7:10:66,554] support the Department's mission in providing medical, dental, and nursing care; active treatment; supervision; education; and  

[7:11:66,565] vocational training for residents with developmental disabilities committed to a state-operated facility.

[9:0:201,422] 4440   Department of State Hospitals  

[10:0:66,443] The Department of State Hospitals manages the nation's largest inpatient forensic mental health hospital system. Its mission is  

[10:1:66,454] to provide evaluation and treatment in a safe and responsible manner, by leading innovation and excellence across a  

[10:2:66,464] continuum of care and settings. The Department is responsible for the daily care and provision of mental health treatment of its  

[10:3:66,474] patients. The Department oversees five state hospitals located in Atascadero, Coalinga, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, and  

[10:4:66,484] Patton,   and employs nearly 13,000 staff. In addition to the state hospital treatment,   the Department provides services in  

[10:5:66,494] contracted jail-based competency treatment (JBCT), community-based restoration (CBR), subacute-capacity and pre-trial  

[10:6:66,505] felony mental health diversion programs, and the conditional release program (CONREP).  

[11:0:66,522] Because the Department programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to  

[11:1:66,532] support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[5:0:66,180] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,199] 4400 - ADMINISTRATION  

[7:0:66,217] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health  

[7:1:66,227] services to patients admitted into Department of State Hospitals facilities. Program Administration includes headquarters  

[7:2:66,237] functions such as: policy development and management, program oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight,  

[7:3:66,247] data research, fiscal, personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services.  

[8:0:66,265] Hospital Administration includes centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care but are administered  

[8:1:66,275] centrally from headquarters.  

[9:0:66,293] 4400010 - HEADQUARTERS ADMINISTRATION  

[10:0:66,311] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health  

[10:1:66,321] services to patients admitted into   its facilities. Headquarters Administration includes headquarters functions such as: policy  

[10:2:66,331] development and management, licensing oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight, data research, fiscal,  

[10:3:66,341] personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services.  

[11:0:66,359] 4400020 - HOSPITAL ADMINISTRATION  

[12:0:66,377] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters includes a Hospital Administration component. Hospital Administration includes  

[12:1:66,387] centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care but are administered centrally from headquarters such as:  

[12:2:66,397] technology services, hospital police and fire oversight, patient referral management, clinical recruitment, patient benefit and  

[12:3:66,407] billing management, and Medicare revenue collection.  

[13:0:66,425] 4410 - STATE HOSPITALS  

[14:0:66,443] The state hospital system includes five state hospitals located at Atascadero, Coalinga, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, and  

[14:1:66,453] Patton. Mental health treatment services at all facilities are delivered by clinical teams who provide full-time inpatient care to  

[14:2:66,463] those with mental illness and those incapable of living in the community. The state hospitals treat the following types of  

[14:3:66,473] patients: civil commitments under the Lanterman-Petris-Short Act (LPS); forensic commitments such as Incompetent to Stand  

[14:4:66,484] Trial (IST), Not Guilty by Reason of Insanity (NGI), Sexually Violent Predators (SVP), and Offender with a Mental Health  

[14:5:66,494] Disorder (OMD); and prisoners with mental illness ( Coleman ) from California Department of Corrections and Rehabilitation  

[14:6:66,504] (CDCR).  

[15:0:66,522] 4410010 - ATASCADERO  

[16:0:66,539] The Department of State Hospitals-Atascadero opened in 1954 and is located on the Central Coast of California in Atascadero  

[16:1:66,550] (San Luis Obispo County). The hospital is a self-contained psychiatric hospital constructed within a security perimeter. The  

[16:2:66,560] majority of the all-male patient population is remanded for treatment by   Superior Courts or by CDCR pursuant to various  

[16:3:66,570] sections of the California Penal Code   and the Welfare and Institutions Code.  

[17:0:66,588] DSH-Atascadero primarily serves the following four patient types: OMD,  Coleman   patients from CDCR, IST, and   NGI.  

[18:0:66,605] 4410020 - COALINGA  

[19:0:66,623] The Department of State Hospitals-Coalinga opened in 2005 and is located on the western edge of Fresno County. The  

[19:1:66,633] hospital is California’s newest forensic mental health hospital and was created to primarily treat SVPs. It is a self-contained  

[19:2:66,643] psychiatric hospital constructed with a security perimeter. CDCR provides perimeter security as well as transportation of  

[19:3:66,654] patients to outside medical services and court proceedings. The majority of the all-male patient population is remanded for  

[19:4:66,664] treatment by   Superior Courts or CDCR pursuant to various sections of the California Penal Code and the Welfare and  

[19:5:66,674] Institutions Code.  

[20:0:66,692] DSH-Coalinga primarily serves SVP, OMD and  Coleman   patients from CDCR.  

[21:0:66,709] 4410030 - METROPOLITAN

[0:0:66,13] 2022-23 STATE BUDGET — HHS   156 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:166,32] 4440   Department of State Hospitals - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The Department of State Hospitals-Metropolitan opened in 1916 and is located in Norwalk (Los Angeles County). The hospital  

[3:1:66,79] is an open style campus with a security perimeter. Due to concerns raised by the community, DSH-Metropolitan maintains a  

[3:2:66,89] formal agreement with the City of Norwalk and the Los Angeles County Sheriff not to accept patients charged with murder or a  

[3:3:66,99] sex crime, or that are at high risk for escape.  

[4:0:66,117] DSH-Metropolitan primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, OMD, and NGI.  

[5:0:66,135] 4410040 - NAPA  

[6:0:66,152] The Department of State Hospitals-Napa opened in 1875 and is located in Napa County. The hospital   was the first of the  

[6:1:66,163] five   State Hospitals and is   the oldest California state hospital still in operation.   It has an open style campus with a security  

[6:2:66,173] perimeter.  

[7:0:66,190] DSH-Napa primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, OMD, and NGI.  

[8:0:66,208] 4410050 - PATTON  

[9:0:66,226] The Department of State Hospitals-Patton opened in 1893 and is located in San Bernardino County. The hospital has an open  

[9:1:66,236] style campus with a security perimeter. CDCR correctional officers provide perimeter security and transportation at DSH-Patton  

[9:2:66,246] as well as transportation of patients to outside medical services and some court proceedings.  

[10:0:66,264] DSH-Patton primarily serves the following five patient types: LPS, IST, OMD, NGI and female  Coleman   patients from CDCR.  

[11:0:66,282] 4410060 - HOSPITAL POLICE OFFICER ACADEMY  

[12:0:66,299] The Department of State Hospitals Police Officer Academy is overseen by the Office of Protective Services, which is a full  

[12:1:66,310] service law enforcement agency that protects the safety and security of the state hospital facilities, staff and patients. The  

[12:2:66,320] Department provides training standards, model programs, cultural competency, program development, and a comprehensive  

[12:3:66,330] training plan to all protective services staff. 

[13:0:66,348] 4420 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM  

[14:0:66,368] The Conditional Release Program is the statewide system of community-based services for specified forensic patients.  

[14:1:66,378] Mandated as a state responsibility by the Governor's Mental Health Initiative of 1984, the program began operations on  

[14:2:66,388] January 1, 1986.  

[15:0:66,406] 4420010 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM  

[16:0:66,424] The Conditional Release Program General/Non-Sexually Violent Predators is comprised of   NGI, OMD, and IST. Individuals  

[16:1:66,434] suitable for this program may be recommended by the state hospital medical director to the courts for outpatient treatment.  

[16:2:66,444] Currently, DSH contracts with seven county-operated and three private organizations   serving all 58 counties in the state with  

[16:3:66,454] non-SVP commitments.  

[17:0:66,472] 4420020 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM -   SEXUALLY VIOLENT PREDATORS  

[18:0:66,490] The Conditional Release Program-Sexually Violent Predators was added to the Conditional Release Program effective January  

[18:1:66,500] 1, 1996 per Welfare and Institutions Code 6604. Prior to the conditional release of the first   SVP in 2003,   conditional release  

[18:2:66,510] providers did not have treatment services that would allow them to accept sexually violent predators as patients, requiring the  

[18:3:66,520] Department of State Hospitals to enter into an annual contract with a single private provider serving 58 counties. Current  

[18:4:66,531] statute requires SVPs be conditionally released to their county of domicile and sufficient funding be available to provide  

[18:5:66,541] treatment and supervision services when an   SVP is conditionally released into the community by court order.  

[19:0:66,559] 4430 - CONTRACTED PATIENT SERVICES  

[20:0:66,576] The Department of State Hospitals contracts with local entities to provide mental health services to some of its patients outside  

[20:1:66,586] of state hospital facilities. This includes the   Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Centers, Jail-Based Competency  

[20:2:66,597] Treatment programs, IST Diversion programs, Community-Based Restoration programs and Sub-Acute Bed Capacity  

[20:3:66,607] programs.  

[21:0:66,625] 4430010 - ADMISSION, EVALUATION, STABILIZATION CENTER 

[22:0:66,642] The Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center in the Kern County Jail receives   IST patients committed to the  

[22:1:66,652] Department of State Hospitals from counties across the state. Patients receive a full evaluation upon admission to determine  

[22:2:66,663] whether they can be treated through the Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center on a short-term basis or may need  

[22:3:66,673] longer-term state hospital treatment. Patients considered to be short-term can be treated and discharged directly from the  

[22:4:66,683] Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center.  

[23:0:66,701] 4430020 - JAIL-BASED COMPETENCY TREATMENT  

[24:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:0:166,32] 4440   Department of State Hospitals - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The Jail-Based Competency Treatment Program focuses on defendants deemed incompetent to stand trial and provides  

[3:1:66,79] mental health treatment to defendants in county jails, restoring them to competency, and allowing for participation in court  

[3:2:66,89] proceedings. 

[4:0:66,107] 4430030 - OTHER CONTRACTED SERVICES  

[5:0:66,124] The Other Contracted Services includes additional contracts with local entities to provide mental health services to some of its  

[5:1:66,135] patients outside of state hospital facilities. Programs include IST Diversion and Community-Based Restoration programs. 

[5:2:66,152] 4430040 - The Other Contracted Services focuses on policy development, program management and oversight of Jail Based  

[5:3:66,163] Treatment Programs and Community Based IST Programs.  

[6:0:66,180] 4430050 - The Jail Based Treatment Programs focus on defendants deemed IST on felony charges and provides mental health  

[6:1:66,190] treatment to these individuals in county jails, restoring them to competency, and allowing for participation in court proceedings.  

[6:2:66,208] 4430060 - The Community Based Incompetent to Stand Trial programs are partnerships with various counties to treat felony  

[6:3:66,218] IST in a community mental health treatment setting. This includes Community-Based Restoration, Diversion and Institutions for  

[6:4:66,229] Mental Diseases Sub-Acute Bed Capacity.  

[6:5:66,246] 4440 - EVALUATION AND FORENSIC SERVICES  

[7:0:66,264] Evaluation and Forensic Services is comprised of the   OMD and the Sex Offender Commitment Programs. Penal Code  

[7:1:66,274] Sections 2960-2981 require that a prisoner who meets specific criteria be ordered by the Board of Parole Hearings to be  

[7:2:66,284] treated by State Hospitals as a condition of parole. The Department of State Hospitals performs evaluations to determine if  

[7:3:66,295] individuals may meet the statutory criteria for the   OMD program. These evaluations are used by the Board of Parole Hearings  

[7:4:66,305] in determining whether a prisoner is committed to the Department of State Hospitals as a condition of parole. Welfare and  

[7:5:66,315] Institutions Code Section 6600 et seq. (Chapter 793, Statutes of 1995) was enacted January 1, 1996, establishing a new  

[7:6:66,325] category of civil commitment for persons found, upon release from prison, to be an SVP. The Sex Offender Commitment  

[7:7:66,335] Program administers clinical screenings and performs evaluations to determine if prisoners may meet the statutory criteria for  

[7:8:66,346] an SVP commitment to the Department of State Hospitals upon completion of their prison term. Superior Courts make the  

[7:9:66,356] ultimate determination whether an individual is likely to be an SVP and warrants forensic psychological evaluations by the  

[7:10:66,366] Department of State Hospitals.  

[8:0:66,384] 4450 - Evaluation and Forensic Services is comprised of the   Offender with a Mental Health Disorder and the Sex Offender  

[8:1:66,394] Commitment Programs as well as the Incompetent to Stand Trial Re-Evaluation Services program.  

[9:0:66,412] 4450010 - The Department is required to provide forensic evaluation services to determine if an inmate within the California  

[9:1:66,422] Department of Corrections and Rehabilitation, prior to parole, requires continued treatment in a state hospital as an Offender  

[9:2:66,432] with a Mental Health Disorder or as a Sexually Violent Predator as a condition of parole. The Department administers these  

[9:3:66,442] services through the Offender with a Mental Health Disorder Program and the Sex Offender Commitment Program.  

[9:4:66,460] 4450020 - The Re-Evaluation Services for Felony Incompetent to Stand Trial program allows the Department to re-evaluate  

[9:5:66,470] individuals deemed felony IST, who have been waiting in jail pending transfer to a Department restoration of competency  

[9:6:66,480] program.

[5:0:66,141] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,160] 4170 - The Commission, established in 2004, provides oversight and accountability for portions of the Mental Health Services  

[6:1:66,170] Act (MHSA), Adult and Older Adult System of Care Act, Children’s Mental Health Services Act, and Mental Health Student  

[6:2:66,180] Services Act. The Commission’s primary roles include:  

[6:3:66,198] Program Review, Oversight and Accountability  

[7:0:66,216] The Commission provides oversight, review, training, technical assistance, accountability, and evaluation of specified mental  

[7:1:66,226] health projects and programs supported with MHSA funds.   This includes review and approval of county mental health  

[7:2:66,236] Innovation Programs   and Expenditure Plans.   It also includes assessing whether services that are provided pursuant to the  

[7:3:66,246] MHSA are cost-effective and in accordance with recommended best practices.  

[7:4:66,264] Policy Projects 

[8:0:66,282] The Commission may advise the Governor and the Legislature regarding actions the state may take to improve care and  

[8:1:66,292] services for   individuals living   with mental illness. The Commission executes projects designed to inform mental health policy by  

[8:2:66,302] integrating research findings and experiential knowledge. The Commission’s projects include criminal justice mental health, the  

[8:3:66,312] state suicide prevention plan, workplace mental health standards, prevention and early intervention strategies, and school-

[8:4:66,322] based mental health.  

[8:5:66,340] Strategic Partnerships  

[9:0:66,358] The Commission partners with universities, institutes, and public agencies to develop, field-test and implement changes and  

[9:1:66,368] policy solutions. The Commission’s partnerships include the Full Service Partnership Pilot, the Early Psychosis Learning Health  

[9:2:66,378] Care Network, the Youth Innovation Project, the Innovation Incubator project, and the suicide crisis center project.  

[9:3:66,396] Grant Programs  

[10:0:66,414] The Commission manages grant programs that incentivize stronger partnerships, integrated services, braided funding and the  

[10:1:66,424] evaluation required for continuous improvement. The Commission’s grant programs include the Mental Health Wellness Act of  

[10:2:66,434] 2013 crisis prevention, early intervention, and crisis response grants, youth drop-in centers, the early psychosis project, and the  

[10:3:66,444] Mental Health Student Services Act.

[2:0:99,32] 4700   Department of Community Services and Development - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The Energy Programs assist low-income households in meeting their immediate and long-term home energy needs through  

[3:1:66,79] financial assistance, energy conservation, weatherization and renewable energy services.  

[4:0:66,97] The Low-Income Home Energy Assistance Program (LIHEAP) provides financial assistance to eligible low-income households  

[4:1:66,107] to offset the costs of heating and/or cooling residential dwellings, assistance for weather-related or energy-related  

[4:2:66,117] emergencies, and weatherization services to improve the energy efficiency of low-income residential dwellings and safeguard  

[4:3:66,127] the health and safety of household occupants. This program may include a leveraging incentive program in which  

[4:4:66,137] supplementary LIHEAP funds can be obtained by LIHEAP grantees if non-federal leveraged home energy resources are used  

[4:5:66,148] along with LIHEAP weatherization related services.  

[5:0:66,165] The Low Income Household Water Assistance Program is designed to provide financial assistance to low-income households  

[5:1:66,175] that pay a high proportion of household income for drinking water and wastewater services, by providing funds to owners or  

[5:2:66,186] operators of public water systems or treatment works to reduce arrearages of, and rates charged to, such households for these  

[5:3:66,196] services.  

[6:0:66,216] The Department of Energy Weatherization Assistance Program provides weatherization to improve the energy efficiency of low-

[6:1:66,226] income residential dwellings and safeguard the health and safety of household occupants.  

[7:0:66,244] The Low-Income Weatherization Program (LIWP) provides energy efficiency and renewable energy services in low-income  

[7:1:66,254] single-family and multi-family dwellings to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and lower energy costs. LIWP projects include  

[7:2:66,265] weatherization and solar photovoltaic systems installations.  

[8:0:66,282] The California Arrearage Payment Program is designed to prevent energy utility disconnections for households experiencing  

[8:1:66,292] financial hardship due to the economic impacts of the COVID-19 pandemic by providing financial assistance to customer  

[8:2:66,303] accounts in arrears.  

[8:3:66,320] 4185 - COMMUNITY SERVICES  

[9:0:66,338] The Community Services Block Grant (CSBG) is designed to enable local government and private nonprofit community  

[9:1:66,348] organizations to help low-income families achieve and maintain economic security through a broad range of activities. These  

[9:2:66,358] activities include education, employment services, emergency services, housing, income support and management, and health  

[9:3:66,369] and nutritional services. Additionally, CSBG funds are used by local community organizations to revitalize low-income  

[9:4:66,379] communities.  

[10:0:66,397] The California Earned Income Tax Credit (CalEITC) benefits low-income, working Californians by providing cash-back tax  

[10:1:66,407] credits to boost the income of eligible individuals and families. Since 2017-18,   the Department   has worked with the Franchise  

[10:2:66,417] Tax Board to provide grant opportunities for community-based organizations to increase awareness of CalEITC.

[9:0:187,518] 4800   California Health Benefit Exchange  

[10:0:66,539] Covered California's mission is to increase the number of insured Californians, improve health care quality, lower costs, and  

[10:1:66,550] reduce health disparities through an innovative, competitive marketplace that empowers consumers to choose the health plan  

[10:2:66,560] and providers that give them the best value.  

[11:0:66,580] Covered California is a public entity within state government with a five-member board appointed by the Governor and  

[11:1:66,590] Legislature. Per Government Code section 100503(o), the board authorizes a budget to pay program expenses from the  

[11:2:66,601] California Health Trust Fund to administer the Exchange.

[12:0:66,550] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[12:1:66,570] 4201 - CALIFORNIA HEALTH BENEFIT EXCHANGE  

[13:0:66,590] Covered California is responsible in part for the implementation of the federal Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act.  

[13:1:66,600] Specifically, it facilitates the enrollment of qualified individuals and small employers in qualified health plans in the individual  

[13:2:66,611] and small employer markets. Eligible consumers can obtain qualified health plan coverage with advance payment of the  

[13:3:66,621] premium tax credit established by the federal Internal Revenue Code.  

[13:4:66,638] 4202 - STATE SUBSIDY PROGRAM  

[14:0:66,656] The State Subsidy Program provides state subsidies through the state-based health insurance exchange to qualified  

[14:1:66,666] individuals with household incomes below 600 percent of the federal poverty level.

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:407,13] 2022-23 STATE BUDGET — HHS   183 

[2:0:170,32] 5160   Department of Rehabilitation - Continued 

[3:0:66,66] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,85] 4210 - VOCATIONAL REHABILITATION SERVICES  

[5:0:66,103] The Vocational Rehabilitation Services Program delivers vocational rehabilitation services to individuals with disabilities through  

[5:1:66,113] vocational rehabilitation professionals in district and branch offices located throughout the state so that individuals with  

[5:2:66,123] disabilities may prepare for and engage in competitive integrated employment and achieve economic self-sufficiency. In  

[5:3:66,133] addition, the Department has cooperative agreements with state and local agencies (secondary and postsecondary education,  

[5:4:66,143] behavioral/mental health, and welfare) to provide services to consumers. The Department operates under a federal Order of  

[5:5:66,154] Selection process, which gives priority to individuals with the most significant disabilities.  

[6:0:66,171] Individuals with disabilities who are eligible for the Department's vocational rehabilitation services may be provided a full range  

[6:1:66,181] of services, including vocational assessment, assistive technology, vocational and educational training, job placement,  

[6:2:66,192] supported employment and independent living skills training to maximize their ability to live and work independently within their  

[6:3:66,202] communities. The Department provides Work Incentives Planning services to reduce dependency on public benefits. The  

[6:4:66,212] Department provides career counseling and information and referral services to encourage individuals working in non-

[6:5:66,222] competitive, non-integrated settings to work toward and achieve competitive integrated employment.  

[7:0:66,240] The Department additionally provides pre-employment transition student services, known as DOR Student Services, and  

[7:1:66,250] auxiliary aids and services necessary to participate in such services to a wide range of students with disabilities, ages 16 up to  

[7:2:66,260] 22 (depending on their exit from their special education program), including many who may benefit from early career  

[7:3:66,271] development. DOR Student Services include job exploration counseling, work-based learning experiences, postsecondary  

[7:4:66,281] education counseling, workplace readiness training, and instruction in self-advocacy. 

[8:0:66,298] The Department, through its Business Enterprises Program, provides comprehensive training and technical assistance to  

[8:1:66,309] enable individuals who are blind or visually impaired to support themselves in the operation of vending stands, snack bars, and  

[8:2:66,319] cafeterias. Prevocational, including employment readiness, services are provided by the Orientation Center for the Blind to  

[8:3:66,329] consumers with vision loss to prepare them for independent living.  

[9:0:66,347] The Department works with public and private organizations to develop and improve community-based vocational rehabilitation  

[9:1:66,357] services for the Department's consumers. The Department sets standards, certifies Community Rehabilitation Programs, and  

[9:2:66,367] establishes fees for services provided to its consumers.  

[10:0:66,385] The Department, in partnership with the Department of Developmental Services, implements strategic initiatives to increase the  

[10:1:66,395] employment of individuals with disabilities through the Disability Employment Program. The Department initiates a targeted  

[10:2:66,405] marketing campaign and incentivizes employers to hire individuals with disabilities through technical assistance, workplace  

[10:3:66,415] accessibility, and support training.  

[11:0:66,433] 4215 - INDEPENDENT LIVING SERVICES  

[12:0:66,451] The Department funds, administers, and supports 28 non-profit independent living centers in communities located throughout  

[12:1:66,461] California. Each independent living center provides services necessary to assist consumers to live independently   with full  

[12:2:66,471] inclusion   in their communities. Core services consist of information and referral, peer counseling, individual and systems  

[12:3:66,481] change advocacy, independent living skills, housing assistance, personal assistance referral services, transition and diversion  

[12:4:66,492] services to community-based living, and   transition services to postsecondary life for youth.  

[13:0:66,509] The Department administers and supports the Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI) Program. In coordination with consumers and their  

[13:1:66,520] families, six service providers throughout California provide a coordinated post-acute care service model for individuals with  

[13:2:66,530] TBI, including supported living, community reintegration, vocational supportive services, public awareness, and support for  

[13:3:66,540] family, friends, and professionals within the TBI community. The Department also works with the federal government to  

[13:4:66,550] administer a TBI partnership grant with which a state TBI Advisory Board has been established for the purpose of creating a  

[13:5:66,560] TBI state plan, sustainability plan, statewide TBI registry, and needs assessment.  

[14:0:66,578] In addition, the Department expands the capacity of existing TBI sites and stand up new TBI sites in alignment with Home and  

[14:1:66,588] Community-Based Services surrounding transition and diversion through community reintegration, personal care services  

[14:2:66,598] through supported living services, and other supportive services to improve functional capabilities of individuals with TBI.  

[15:0:66,616] The Department administers the federal Older Individuals Who Are Blind program that supports 17 non-profit community-based  

[15:1:66,626] organizations throughout California that provide blindness-related independent living services necessary to assist visually  

[15:2:66,637] impaired consumers age 55 or older to live independently and be productive in their communities. Core services consist of low  

[15:3:66,647] vision evaluations/screenings, assistive technology devices and training, orientation and mobility, communication skills,  

[15:4:66,657] independent living skills training, self-advocacy, adjustment counseling, transportation, and supportive services.  

[16:0:66,675] Through a partnership with the California Public Utilities Commission’s Deaf and Disabled Telecommunications Program, the  

[16:1:66,685] Department’s Voice Options program provides eligible Californians who are unable to speak, or who have difficulty speaking,  

[16:2:66,695] with a free speech-generating device. The goal of this program is to ensure full and equal telephone communications access  

[16:3:66,705] for all Californians with disabilities.  

[17:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[11:1:66,548] 4250 - STATE COUNCIL SERVICES  

[12:0:66,568] The State Independent Living Council is responsible for developing a state plan for independent living and for monitoring,  

[12:1:66,578] reviewing and evaluating the implementation of that plan. The Council also interacts with similar statewide councils to enhance  

[12:2:66,588] the effectiveness of the network of centers that provide independent living services in California. The Council is required by the

[12:4:66,609] Services and the Centers for Independent Living. The Council serves as an educational resource on disability and independent

[2:0:144,32] 5175   Department of Child Support Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,66] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,85] 4260 - CHILD SUPPORT SERVICES PROGRAM  

[4:0:66,103] The Child Support Services program establishes the system and process for encouraging and, when necessary, enforcing  

[4:1:66,113] parental responsibilities by establishing paternity for children, establishing court orders for financial and medical support, and  

[4:2:66,123] enforcing those orders. The program operates as the single state entity designed to administer the federally mandated Title IV-

[4:3:66,133] D child support program in California. Operation of this program is required for the state to continue to receive the Temporary  

[4:4:66,143] Assistance for Needy Families block grant.  

[4:5:66,161] 4260010 - CHILD SUPPORT ADMINISTRATION:  

[5:0:66,179] The Child Support Administration program provides funding for the salaries and benefits for local and state staff, and operating  

[5:1:66,189] expenses and equipment for the operation of California's child support program, including local child support agencies. The  

[5:2:66,199] federal government provides 66 percent of the funding and the state funds 34 percent of the administration costs.  

[5:3:66,217] 4260019 - CHILD SUPPORT AUTOMATION:  

[6:0:66,235] Pursuant to Federal law, the Department created a single, statewide child support automation system that meets federal  

[6:1:66,245] certification. There are two components of the statewide system: the Child Support Enforcement system and the State  

[6:2:66,255] Disbursement Unit. The enforcement system provides local child support staff tools to manage child support customer accounts  

[6:3:66,265] and locate and intercept assets of non-custodial parents delinquent in their child support payments. The Child Support  

[6:4:66,275] Automation program provides funding for the vendor-operated state disbursement unit, which collects child support payments  

[6:5:66,286] from non-custodial parents and disburses payments to custodial parties. In addition, the Child Support Automation program  

[6:6:66,296] provides funding for electronic data processing maintenance and operation costs at local agencies.
